<div id="review_150044517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150044517" />
    <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes"><img alt="Nancy Oakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507555979p2/900340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150044517?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Oakes" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes">Nancy Oakes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846554001" href="/book/show/8687803-the-leopard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=translated-crime-fiction">translated-crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=crime-fiction-scandinavia">crime-fiction-scandinavia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150044517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15565975429431459134">It is just a crying shame that this novel is not going to be available in the U.S. right away, because really, American readers of Jo Nesbø are missing out on one of the very best books in the entire series. I couldn't even purchase a copy from Book Depository directly, so I had to take the roundabout alternative and purchase from BD through Amazon. It's a bit more expensive, but well worth it. Trust me, after finishing The Snowman, you are going to want to read this book as quickly as possible.</span>
  <span id="freeText15565975429431459134" style="display:none">It is just a crying shame that this novel is not going to be available in the U.S. right away, because really, American readers of Jo Nesbø are missing out on one of the very best books in the entire series. I couldn't even purchase a copy from Book Depository directly, so I had to take the roundabout alternative and purchase from BD through Amazon. It's a bit more expensive, but well worth it. Trust me, after finishing The Snowman, you are going to want to read this book as quickly as possible. <br /><br />In fact, in this episode of the Harry Hole series, the story picks up shortly after the events of The Snowman, which (without giving too much away) took their physical and emotional toll on Harry, sending him as far away from Norway and the police department as possible to Hong Kong. There he lives in squalor, bets money he doesn't have on the horses and runs up serious debts that prevent him from leaving the country. He also discovers that opium lessens his pain and allows him to stay away from the booze. But events back in Norway soon require his presence, and Detective Kaja Solness has come to Hong Kong to collect him and bring him back to Oslo. Harry adamantly refuses, but then relents when it turns out that his father is seriously ill and in the hospital. When he returns, he discovers that there's another serial killer on the loose, a person who has killed two people in a most gruesome fashion and leaves behind no evidence. More murders occur, but he's facing an even tougher problem. His colleagues in the Crime Squad, are in a fight with the Kripos (Krimpolitisentralen) over control of murder investigations, a battle that involves not just the two rival groups, but the future careers of many of Harry's colleagues and even Harry himself. The Kripos have taken jurisdiction over this series of murders, and the investigation is in the hands of Bellman -- a politico who is all about power and control, as opposed to Harry, who wants to solve the case and bring the perpetrator to justice. While this situation complicates matters for the Crime Squad, it doesn't stop Harry from doing his own investigation. Harry gets unofficial assistance from some of his colleagues, as well as some clandestine help from an old friend to figure out what it is that connects the victims together. Once he figures this out, he believes, it will help him with the who and the why. But this is not going to be easy. It will take all that Harry has to give, which right now isn't that much, and will take him back and forth across the globe before his job is done.<br /><br />The character of Harry Hole is quite possibly at his best in this novel, even though emotionally he's at his lowest point. He has become a very real person here, battling through his personal demons which makes him a bit reckless and often prone to acting without thinking. He warns others who want to work with him that it is his pattern to drag them down alongside himself, and he is not wrong. But despite all of his personal issues, Harry is the consummate detective, and will not let go of the case until it is finished, no matter what means he has to use to get the job done. <br /><br />Nesbø has done an incredible job with The Leopard, and readers of crime fiction, especially those who have followed Nesbø's series from the beginning, will in no way be disappointed. He is able to peak the reader's interest at the very start of the novel with a most nasty crime and a bad guy who has absolutely no conscience, then ratchet up the tension level little by little until it is impossible to put the book down. His plotting is meticulous, but it is his attention to detail, the addition of the tension between the two police groups, and above all his portrayal of Harry Hole on a most human level that makes this story work and work well. There are also several references to Hole's other cases here and there throughout the story, bringing to mind all that this man has been through.<br /><br />The Leopard is incredibly long, and I found some of it a bit confusing at times, especially regarding one of the subplots of the novel. It moves slowly in several parts to the point where you think you might be trying to crawl through jello. And yes, there are some very over-the-top moments that Nesbø seems to enjoy throwing into each one of his novels that make the action a little hard to swallow sometimes. However, it is probably my favorite of the series, and although it took some time to read, it was well worth every second. I started this on an airplane, and as much as I hate flying, I forgot where I was for the entire 5 hours because I was so caught up in the story. Do not make The Leopard your introduction to the Harry Hole series -- if nothing else, at least read The Snowman, so you will have an understanding of Harry's mindset going into this one, which is in many ways the continuation of the latter. Better yet, start with The Redbreast and read your way through one of the best crime fiction series currently available. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15565975429431459134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

And I am so sorry for it, girls, but I hope you enjoy it and forgive me!<br><br><br></i></span>

<div id="review_245738478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/245738478" />
    <a title="F.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1309606-f-r"><img alt="F.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544886612p2/1309606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/245738478?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="F.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="F.R." href="/user/show/1309606-f-r">F.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099548973" href="/book/show/9639166-the-leopard">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer245738478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4264619661241148139">So the advertising does work. One finds it almost impossible to commute around London these days without seeing adverts for Jo Nesbo’s various thrillers. They give the impression that every sentient being on the planet is currently gripped by this man’s books and slavering for the next one. More than eating or breathing oxygen, reading Norwegian crime novels is <i>the</i> done thing for the human race right now. As such, because I appear to be more of a sucker for this kind of thing than I previously r</span>
  <span id="freeText4264619661241148139" style="display:none">So the advertising does work. One finds it almost impossible to commute around London these days without seeing adverts for Jo Nesbo’s various thrillers. They give the impression that every sentient being on the planet is currently gripped by this man’s books and slavering for the next one. More than eating or breathing oxygen, reading Norwegian crime novels is <i>the</i> done thing for the human race right now. As such, because I appear to be more of a sucker for this kind of thing than I previously realised, I have picked up another one. Even though I found its predecessor, ‘The Snowman’, somewhat derivative, I have now made my way through ‘The Leopard’.<br /><br />And I have to say I‘m still not convinced.<br /><br />For a start the opening is preposterous. Harry Hole – our hero – has now become an opium addict in Hong Kong, and rather than leave him there to rot, the Norwegian police sends a young female officer to bring him back and get him to lead a high-profile investigation. Now, would any real police force seriously do this? If a once decorated officer has gone so far off the rails they are now living high as a kite in the hinterlands of a far away country, surely their former employers is not going to demand that they come back and take on an actual investigation. What would the press say after all? It’s the kind of thing which happens in movies starring a Mel Gibson or a Sylvester Stallone, but in a supposedly ‘real world’ crime thriller requires the sensitive reader to swallow a huge amount of disbelief.<br /><br />The ending – again set away from Oslo – is also quite ludicrous (although I won’t spoil that for anyone). While in-between is a quite interesting police investigation into the customarily over-the-top serial killer. There’s a lot of gore, some fun red-herrings, but certainly more inter-departmental politics than this particular reader would have liked. <br /><br />It’s dumb, but not an actively bad book – I just don’t see what other people are getting so excited about.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4264619661241148139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16102801831065395594" style="display:none">it starts slowly around middle I was enjoying some nice plot twist, but after that it went shockingly bad. things I did not enjoy:<br />- made up torture devices are ok, but presenting them as a real historical artefact stinks<br />- Norwegian police routinely travel to civil-war plagued African countries to investigate on a whim, without any official liason, contact, legal backup, guns, preparation or even a fucking medical check.<br />Nesbo is trying too hard and puts too many locations (rwanda, hong kong, germany, kongo...) the best part of the book the book takes place on a snowy plains in small tourist huts. Who would have guessed that from a nordic writer? all the extra locations are useless. in Snowman Nesbo tried to compensate for lack of polished writing by weirdness and cruelty. In Leopard he compensates by geographic location and cruelty<br />- the climax was astonishingly pathetic. Shoot out on a top of a volcano? I smell bad 80s Dolph Lundgren action movies. So next time keep it simple, keep it in Norway, do not make shit up, try to be realistic</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=mystery-detective-thriller">mystery-detective-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=nordic-noir">nordic-noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3552078186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11444184643729900002">Book #8 of the Harry Hole series is set in Norway, one of the richest, happiest and safest places in the world, where Jo Nesbo must convince us horrific murders take place there. My suspicion is that he is hired by the Promote Norway Program by discouraging visitors from moving there. The story also moves to Goma, Congo, though it opens in Hong Kong, where Harry has fled the life of detectiving and his relationship to Rakel after the traumatizing events of The Snowman, his last book (because twi</span>
  <span id="freeText11444184643729900002" style="display:none">Book #8 of the Harry Hole series is set in Norway, one of the richest, happiest and safest places in the world, where Jo Nesbo must convince us horrific murders take place there. My suspicion is that he is hired by the Promote Norway Program by discouraging visitors from moving there. The story also moves to Goma, Congo, though it opens in Hong Kong, where Harry has fled the life of detectiving and his relationship to Rakel after the traumatizing events of The Snowman, his last book (because twice now his work has endangered her and her son Oleg, who sees HH as his father). Is he trying to heal or flush his life down the toilet in Hong Kong? Well, he's an alcoholic, he’s not drinking there, but he is taking opium in measured doses, and gambling, and not much else. He returns to Oslo because the Oslo police have another killing spree they think might be the work of a serial killer, and (mainly) because Harry’s father is dying. For a thriller, it’s probably a five star book, but let me explain my taking a star off in my random notes, which I share rather than a detailed plot synopsis.<br /><br />*The book opens as Nesbo follows Elmore Leonard’s advice and does NOT feature the weather, but a sadistic, disturbing murder scene: A woman sits in a chair with what appears to be an s/m gag in her mouth tied to razor wire that will kill her if she moves. Nesbo calls this invention of his own devising a Leopold’s Apple. I decide to finish the book but never read another woman, as this moment (like many in The Snowman and several others in this book) amount to torture porn. Not into it. Angry. <br /><br />*And he’s now written three books of eight featuring serial killers. Instead of drawn in the plot, I wonder how thrill-killer writers will up the ante to get readers’ attention? Nesbo says, well, I had one serial killer in The Snowman, so I will introduce you to multiple ones in The Leopard! Yay! (Not a spoiler in that I am not saying how others are involved, exactly).<br /><br />*Nesbo wants to focus on what it is to be a man here. He would appear to hate it that many women like gorgeous alpha-male assholes, so he sets up a contrast; the gorgeous, anti-hero, damaged, alcoholic vulnerable Harry Hole in this corner, and the gorgeous, ambitious, Mikael Bellman (who is like last book’s Tom Waaler, a Baywatch type guy). Kaja, who it would seem may be vying to be a replacement for Rakel to Harry, actually chooses Mikael, initially, which is unfortunate. But Bellman, unforgiving, no complex, would never forgive Kaja for this; Harry does, and agrees to even work with Bellman. TO be flawed is what Harry is. We like him as a man even though he is anguished and a kind of mess a lot of the time. Both Bellman and Hole (as Dirty Harry) will break the law to catch the killers, but Bellman just wants to get ahead, and HH only wants to catch the killers.<br /><br />*I read Ian Fleming’s Bonds and HH seems a little like Bond in that hey both are subjected to extreme and sadistic torture and they survive peril after peril again and again. James Bond is a perfect hero; Harry Hole is not, but they are both typical thriller main characters, hero or not. Hole is just more of an anti-hero for our realistic time.<br /><br />*Harry uses a surprising accomplice to solve the crime (spoiler alert): The dying Snowman.<br /><br />*There’s a father-son theme running through this one, too. The killer had a sadistic father. Harry has flaws he sees in his dying father. Can we ever learn, and overcome the flaws of our fathers?<br /><br />* I decide to read the next one because of The Human Interest angle: Rakel sees Harry at the funeral, after which he heads back to Hong Kong. But will he ever learn and heal and become worthy of her and be a father figure to Oleg? I’m a sucker, not for the torture, but the love angle here, though it is a long shot, truly.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11444184643729900002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2148877351" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2148877351" />
    <a title="Katherine " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68791099-katherine"><img alt="Katherine " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504607541p2/68791099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2148877351?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine " href="/user/show/68791099-katherine">Katherine </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846554018" href="/book/show/9911085-the-leopard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68791099-katherine?shelf=murder-mystery-crime">murder-mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68791099-katherine?shelf=original">original</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68791099-katherine?shelf=tough-stuff">tough-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2148877351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13944894937209801666">This is the third Jo Nesbo book I've read and I must say that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/904719.Jo_Nesb_' title='Jo Nesbø' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jo Nesbø</a> deserves all the hype he gets. <br/><br/>Traumatized by the snowman case Harry flees to Thailand to drown into his inner demons until his colleagues drag him back to Norway to help with a new case and inform him that his father is sick. <br/><br/>The new serial killer is much different than the snowman, different motives, different killing style and personality which I appreciated and I thought was believable - this story could actually happen s</span>
  <span id="freeText13944894937209801666" style="display:none">This is the third Jo Nesbo book I've read and I must say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/904719.Jo_Nesb_" title="Jo Nesbø" rel="nofollow noopener">Jo Nesbø</a> deserves all the hype he gets. <br /><br />Traumatized by the snowman case Harry flees to Thailand to drown into his inner demons until his colleagues drag him back to Norway to help with a new case and inform him that his father is sick. <br /><br />The new serial killer is much different than the snowman, different motives, different killing style and personality which I appreciated and I thought was believable - this story could actually happen somewhere. <br /><br />I like the cultural depth that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/904719.Jo_Nesb_" title="Jo Nesbø" rel="nofollow noopener">Jo Nesbø</a> goes into in his books, not just about Norway but Belgium and the Congo and just the details he likes to decorate his stories with - they make a world of difference when your visualizing the story in your mind. <br /><br />I love <b> Harry </b> as a character and especially enjoyed learning more about his relationship with his father and family. He loves them and appreciates them very much but has a very personal and private way of showing it and so do his friends. I agree with him in the sense that you don't need to be hugging someone every second of the day to show them you love them being there can be enough and the fact that he made a point to see his father almost every night was sentimental enough for me and suits him as a character. <br /><br />He moved through the case in an expected pace given that he wasn't sober half the time and once again showed us how selfless he really is. I love that he doesn't care about credit and just focuses on getting the job done. <br /><br />Also it was great seeing him with <b> Katrine </b> again - shes my favorite female character so far - genius, crazy and funny. All the other women in his books seem very blah and to be honest boring.<br /><br />This <b> Kaja chick </b> was borderline annoying with her neediness and predicable behavior. Like you were just in love with Bellman now you wanna marry Harry? Of course your not enough reason for him to stay, what you guys banged twice and you think he cant live without you? have you not been paying attention? he can live without anybody that's the point!<br /><br />I get that Nesbo likes to always have a girl for Harry - kind of like a bond girl but truly this is the only reason why I'm giving this book 4 stars and not 5. Every other aspect was excellent. The philosophy, the story, the unfolding of the plot - all perfect. <br /><br />But you don't need sex scenes or love stories in every book. Harry and Kayas (Kaja?) relationship was very robotic and uninteresting and in my opinion completely unnecessary. It did nothing for the story or his character - it only bored me every time I had to read about it. <br /><br />Overall the messages of mercy, survival, selfishness and selflessness were beautifully portrayed, the writing was excellent and I love Jo Nesbo. I love Harry Hole and I recommend this book to those who like crime stories and thrillers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13944894937209801666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1133169961" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133169961" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133169961?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133169961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15340360851092215819">By crafting arguably the most intense of the Harry Hole novels to date, Nesbø puts the reader in the middle of an intense murder investigation and search for another horrific killer. After suffering greatly at the hands of the The Snowman, a serial killer from a previous novel, Hole is hiding out in Hong Kong, with little interest in returning to his native land. Kaja Solness, newest member of the Crime Squad within the Oslo Police, is sent to coax him back, explaining that the Squad has come up</span>
  <span id="freeText15340360851092215819" style="display:none">By crafting arguably the most intense of the Harry Hole novels to date, Nesbø puts the reader in the middle of an intense murder investigation and search for another horrific killer. After suffering greatly at the hands of the The Snowman, a serial killer from a previous novel, Hole is hiding out in Hong Kong, with little interest in returning to his native land. Kaja Solness, newest member of the Crime Squad within the Oslo Police, is sent to coax him back, explaining that the Squad has come upon a potential new serial killer whose methods are horrific. Solness is only able to convince Hole when she reveals that his father, Olev, is dying in hospital. Upon his return to Norway, Hole realises that the Crime Squad is in a significant power struggle with Kripos, the national police service, which investigates serious crimes. Its head, Mikael Bellman, has no love loss for Hole and tries to contain the former investigator. Hole only becomes involved in the investigation when a Norwegian MP is killed, at which point he is convinced her death is closely related to the other two murders. Working undercover with members of the Squad, Hole begins poking around and determines that there is a common denominator, a cabin at which all the victims stayed on the same night. Working closely with Solness not only creates great workplace chemistry, but allows Hole to get closer to her on a more personal level, even if it backfires for a time. When the Squad's antics are uncovered by Bellman, they scatter and Hole is eventually brought on to work with Kripos as a consultant of sorts. Hole and Bellman concoct a sting operation at the cabin with one of the potential victims who's fled to Australia. However, when the killer outsmarts everyone, things take another turn for the worse. An arrest by Kripos of the potential killer goes horribly wrong when an airtight alibi is given and Hole is left holding the blame. It is only when Hole visits The Snowman in prison that he obtains a means of approaching the case that might help. After using that advice, Hole cracks the case wide open and learns just how sinister this serial killer is prone to be, using something called a Leopold's Apple to assist with slayings. With time spent in Congo as well as throughout Norway, Hole and the rest of the characters weave a thrilling tale matched only in Nesbø's other wonderful Harry Hole thrillers.<br /><br />The progression of the series is masterful on so many levels. Hole becomes more despondent as the books progress, digging himself deeper into his own personal isolation chamber, though his character is such that readers can find many parallels or likeable aspects. Nesbø is certain to allow much growth in his characters and builds on Hole's complexities throughout the series, as well as weaving storylines from past novels into each subsequent one, which forces the reader to be sharp and use the power of recollection. As with many of the novels, the former love of Hole's life, Rakel, makes an appearance and pulls on his limited heartstrings in such a way that he cannot shake her, no matter how hard he tries. There is even some personal growth on Hole's immediate family front, where both sister and father play a limited by significant role in the larger narrative. Readers who enjoy the series will likely use this book (and its predecessor) as the standard against which all other series novels are judged. Stellar work keeping the story moving and the reader hooked throughout.<br /><br />Kudos Mr. Nesbø for always finding new ways to impress your readers. 'What will Hole do next?', sits on the tip of my tongue when I begin each new novel.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15340360851092215819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_238927808" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238927808" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277905205p2/1166663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238927808?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846554001" href="/book/show/8687803-the-leopard">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carol by: </span>
      publisher, ARC
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238927808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4135891314877475147">I'm a latecomer to the Harry Hole Norwegian thrillers but am becoming a fan of the series and of author, Jo Nesbo. I thought The Snowman was grisly and taut but compared to The Leopard, it’s like a walk in the park. Nesbo definitely steps up the violence a notch. Not all readers will be appreciative of this but as long as I’m just reading and not the victim, I’m ok with this. <br/><br/>In the Leopard we find Hole, holed up in Hong Kong making very little attempt to get his life back together. He is wallow</span>
  <span id="freeText4135891314877475147" style="display:none">I'm a latecomer to the Harry Hole Norwegian thrillers but am becoming a fan of the series and of author, Jo Nesbo. I thought The Snowman was grisly and taut but compared to The Leopard, it’s like a walk in the park. Nesbo definitely steps up the violence a notch. Not all readers will be appreciative of this but as long as I’m just reading and not the victim, I’m ok with this. <br /><br />In the Leopard we find Hole, holed up in Hong Kong making very little attempt to get his life back together. He is wallowing in something; grief, guilt, whatever you call it, up to his eyeballs. His spiral of destruction involves a whole lot of drinking, drugging, who gives a….this after fiancée, Rakel and her son leave Harry when they find they are used as pawns in Harry’s encounter with The Snowman. But Harry’s soon to be pulled out of his blackness, like it or not. His former boss sends an attractive young detective, Kaja Solness, to drag his sorry behind back to Norway and solve yet another string of serial murders. Avalanching the plot forward is a side story about his father, a reunion with his sister, an intricate plot that somehow works, gruesome devices that kill, and the cold, continually bleak Norwegian setting and you’ve got another winner. <br /><br />In the end, plot twists, mystery, gore, these are not the things that attract me to Harry Hole. He’s just so dismal that you’ve got to love him. Let’s hope he’s truly not going to retire and that he’ll take up the cause of fighting evil once again. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4135891314877475147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7WjmvTcCL/77547WrfAAONccQvhWARtMl7apXBIyPV48Yf+nJzn8ysqzaKehVhY/DFIGppEX8/86KXJQ9fGang==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NjxqfqKJQiLw5T1XA2sgUB9TTQH99jC47Hr0QFp843znNXNksrKRFsGx2yYPzTZXxB0JXzrg2AtB5S9Mvb9EvA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer132228056272078886">Jo Nesbø is a bestselling Norwegian author and musician. He was born in Oslo and grew up in Molde. Nesbø graduated from the Norwegian School of Economics with a degree in economics. Nesbø is primarily famous for his crime novels about Detective Harry Hole, but he is also the main vocals and songwriter for the Norwegian rock band Di Derre. In 2007 Nesbø also released his first children's book, Dokt</span>
  <span id="freeText132228056272078886" style="display:none">Jo Nesbø is a bestselling Norwegian author and musician. He was born in Oslo and grew up in Molde. Nesbø graduated from the Norwegian School of Economics with a degree in economics. Nesbø is primarily famous for his crime novels about Detective Harry Hole, but he is also the main vocals and songwriter for the Norwegian rock band Di Derre. In 2007 Nesbø also released his first children's book, Doktor Proktors Prompepulver.<br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51155-harry-hole" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Hole</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/66741-doktor-proktor" rel="nofollow noopener">Doktor Proktor</a><br /><br />For exclusive content about Jo Nesbø and his books, register for the official fan newsletter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://jonesbo.com/newsletter/">https://jonesbo.com/newsletter/</a></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_32775291').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_32775291').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_32775291').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
